< Review>
With so many great options for ramen in LA, it can be hard to find a spot that brings it. Iki ramen kills it. The LATimes review via Eater LA brought me and a friend here.

They recommended the burnt garlic bowl, and so would I. Although the broth is what I went for, the perfectly al dente noodles would bring me back. We were also a big fan of the pork bun. I dare to say that it was even better than the ramen. We also tried the crispy rice tuna appetizer. It was so close to being perfect. I loved the fresh tuna and the marinade, but the rice was ever so slightly too crispy.

The decor was minimalistic and cozy. The room itself was small, just like most ramen joints. It can be a little loud if every table is filled, but not unbearable.

Overall, I enjoyed my meal here and I would definitely come back if I were craving ramen in KTown.</Review>

< userid>
117872276526090591694< /userid>
<user_name>Nicholas Dobkin</user_name>< time>
1583731474475< /time>
<Rate>5</Rate><Text>Common wisdom has always held that however good Koreatown ramen was, it would always be second to the more iconic ramens of Little Tokyo and Sawtelle. With the recent arrival of a branch of Silverlake Ramen seeming to take top spot, it seemed like Ktown would forever live in the shadow of better ramen. Iki strikes out at that misconception with vigor, proving that breadth and depth of flavor can go hand in hand and in so doing, easily becoming one of the top ramen shops in Los Angeles.

Most ramen shops focus on doing one thing really well, whether it's the typical rich tonkotsu that anyone would like, or a specific niche that you can't get elsewhere. Iki kicks this cliche to the curb by creating a menu tailored to almost every taste in ramens, while never sacrificing the quality of the dishes.

For those seeking a rich pork broth, you'll want to go for the Burnt Garlic Tonkotsu. The smell alone outs it as the real deal, a tremendous broth full of savor. The eggs are perfectly cooked to occupy the glass-like medium texture between hard and melted yokes, making for a flavorful soft treasure of an egg. The pork is incredible, balancing crispy outsides juicy soft insides. The noodles are thin and hard, which isn't to my taste, but some will enjoy it and it certainly can't come close to ruining the dish. All alone this would be a worthy ramen for some. But it doesn't stop here.

For those seeking a lighter broth, iki has a refreshingly zesty yuzu shoyu. As a tonkotsu person myself I actually found the yuzu broth a bit of an acquired taste, but I know there will be people who love it. The interesting thing is that the noodle type for this bowl was different - a chewier wider noodle I enjoyed more.

It keeps going. Iki has vegan options in the form of its miso ramen and tan tan mazemen (soupless) which use impossible meat. I went with a vegan friend who said she enjoyed it although she noted that for those who want food which doesn't resemble meat, the dish is meant to resemble real pork visually, though she said she could distinguish the taste. Even so she liked the dish overall.

And just when you think you're done, Iki hits an absolute home run with it's desserts. Fans of black sesame will adore their creamy black sesame creme brulee, oozing with sesame flavor under it's freshly carmelized top layer. But my absolute favorite, possibly one of the best desserts I've ever had, was their yuzu ice cream. Smooth and citrusy, the cream is balanced by a sprinkle of brown palm sugar which adds a light crunch and incredible burst of flavor. It is truly an experience not to be missed for anyone looking for a great ice cream.

I haven't even dug through half the menu and when I think of their chicken paitan, special winter truffle butter and assortment of others, I can't avoid thinking of Iki as the menu that keeps giving. Parking is manageable and close, and lines are practically non-existant despite the shop being relatively small. The only reason K can see for this is that somehow no one knows Iki is here so if that describes you, here's the takeaway: Iki is the rising star of ramen in KTown - no matter what taste you bring to their table, you're sure to find something to love!</Text>< Pics>

#claysramengame on Instagram alertüö®!!
We have a contender for at the very least, the best bowl in ktown and at the very most, IN TOWN! Iki Ramen is brand spankin‚Äô new but it sure does deliver! This place is designer friendly in both the craft of their light and crispy broths as well in their decor. This was the yuzu shio, of which only one other place in town has, but there it‚Äôs just so so.  One of the ELUSIVE 5 BOWL RATING bowls I had in Harajuku was also a yuzu shio. Man, what a tasty broth with the appropriate, albeit standard, noodle. The chashu was freaking soft and decadent and the menma was fresh and not overpowering.  The shoyu, not pictured, was also very good. The wait staff was nice and accommodating as well. Only pet peeve was when the waiter wasn‚Äôt able to let me know where they get their noodles from. As far as Japanese owners, I‚Äôm not sure, but I think there was a mix of Korean and Japanese in the kitchen. The waiter, not Japanese, also couldn‚Äôt understand when we wanted ‚Äúkaedama‚Äù extra noodles which is on the menu, so those were two slight strikes. I suppose the presentation could have been a bit better as well, which makes me think it isn‚Äôt a full Japanese kitchen because presentation, even in how the noodles are set, is very meticulously done in legit Japanese ramen. This place was slightly lacking that aesthetic. That being said, very solid spot, great desserts too! Headed back soon!!! It gets ever so close to an ELUSIVE 5 BOWL RATING with a 4.5 bowl rating! üçúüçúüçúüçú.5 #tonkotsu #shio #shoyu #chopsticks #broth #chashu #ramen #noodle #yuzu #ikiramen< /text>

I just had the yuzu shio ramen and it is the most elegant ramen I've ever had. Never imagined I'd use elegance to describe ramen but it was light, beautiful and perfectly balanced with the decadence of the slow braised pork belly. I get the feeling the chef has fine dining experience: as thoughtful details abound throughout the minimal chic restaurant with warm subdued attentive service.
My friend and I shared the black sesame creme br√ªl√©e for dessert. Pronounced sesame flavor with a perfect level of sweetness (not overtly sweet like most desserts are).
My new favorite ramen place... I will definitely be back to try the rest of the menu.< /review>

<review>New hip place in ktown for some ramen with great classics and twists from your usual tonkotsu. I love salmon, heard their quality is quite good, so I had to try some!

SALMON
Salmon Burrata  -- I had high hopes from reading reviews about this but thought it was so-so. Salmon wasn't incredible but burrata was rich and creamy. I thought there could be less yuzu flavor so the honey truffle could really shine.

Salmon ikura bowl -- I had this one for delivery on a separate day. I thought the salmon quality was so so again. But the rice was good and portion size was good. More salmon than the burrata dish, even at the same price, though this bowl was super simple and exactly was as the name says.

We tried each others' food cause friends, and general consensus :
RAMEN
- Tori paitan broth tastes like ham?
- Garlic tonkotsu has strong garlic flavor. Still good with depth in the flavor.
-Yuzu Shio was a favorite. Broth is flavorful and the yuzu cuts the richness of the ramen. Yuzu adds a slight fresh taste to ramen.

DESSERT
- Shio Koji Ice Cream - What is that? Get it.
Rich milky ice cream with tones of caramel. It was unique but familiar at the same time. Shio Koji is fermented rice (hey probiotics, it's like froyo now) but really don't let the fermented funk deter you from getting this. It's not sour at all. Especially if salted caramel ice cream is your flava!
-Yuzu ice cream - very lemony, this was too citrusy for me but friend really liked it.
-Black sesame creme brulee - classic with a twist! Popular in our group. Though Shio Koji was my fav!

I guess one thing that could be improved is phone communication?
Ok they really do not pick up their phone. Our group was kinda big (6 ppl) so I called a few times to ask if they took reservations -- after several days trying,  someone finally picked up, said "no" very bluntly and hung up. It felt like recieving a "kk" but in a call. Ok... Thanks...! Just wanted to ask.

But in person it was better. I came early to grab our party a table, luckily they put some tables together and easily we were all seated! Our server was kind and attentive throughout. :) It's not a big place and the place definitely got busy especially after 7 on sunday evening. They have a parking lot but shared amongst other businesses, it was definitely limited.</review><Pictures>None</Pictures><Resp>None<//Resp>< GmapID>

<text>My first visit here was great. Their yuzu and burnt garlic ramen were both delicious! Yuzo shio ramen was very light and refreshing. It was great to share with the burnt garlic ramen which had a much richer broth and spicier.

Would also recommend takoyaki and croquette appetizers to share. However, I would NOT recommend the salmon yuzu appetizer. It tasted fine, but... it was just OK and cost $10 for 4 slices of salmon with some yuzu sauce drizzled. Way over priced. On the other hand, takoyaki was only $4!

Service was great the first time I was here. Second time, it was much busier. Food still came out relatively quickly and service was good, but it took way too long to get the bill. More training on POS system needed.

Overall, love that they have some unique ramen flavors and would definitely come back!

Parking is available in the plaza though it's not a big lot . Kung Fu tea is next door for boba after. Extra points.</text>< Pictures>

<text>No reservation needed or possible, it‚Äôs a first come first serve. To find a spot you‚Äôll have to drive through the campgrounds. It helps to have one person get out of the car and read the permits, sometimes previous occupants forget to take their permits off the site markers, so it‚Äôs easy to think the site is occupied. Once you‚Äôve found your desired site, park(each site has it‚Äôs own parking spot). Make sure you take a picture of your license plate and remember your site number. Head back towards the entrance of the camp grounds, in front of the info board you‚Äôll find the permits you‚Äôll need to register for you site, oh yes make sure you have a pen too, and exact change, cause you‚Äôll be depositing payment into a slot. I didn‚Äôt have exact change, and wasn‚Äôt able to find staff around.

I recommend arriving well before evening, so you‚Äôre not setting up tent in the dark and with bugs. Beautiful meadow view. Restroom well stocked with toilet paper, trash was emptied daily, clean except for the bugs, but what do you expect, it‚Äôs better than porta-potties, functional soap dispensers and sinks with hot water.

What I loved about this campground was that each site has a parking spot and it‚Äôs own fire pit and some even have benches nearby. You‚Äôre allowed to burn any downed wood, twigs, pine cones around, NOT TRASH.  There are dumpsters around to dump trash. Tons of cute spots to take pictures.

Also some sites might be hard to accommodate more than one car, there‚Äôs a parking lot next to the campgrounds.

One last thing, I have sprint and the reception SUCKED, I was only able to receive and make calls. But luckily we didn‚Äôt need phone service, just make sure you check the weather & maybe make a make available offline if you‚Äôre maps dependent.</text><gmap_id>0x8097483b80d22415:0x63885f0a58a71dd< /gmap_id><date>1595562498680< /date>< user>

<review>Pretty nice $30 first come first serve no reservation campground about 3/4 mile from Pinecrest Lake.  About 3/4 mile walk to the lake depending on camp site.  Flush toilets with lights, but only a few for the whole campground.  Good fresh water from spigots.  Trees are slowly dying away leaving less and less shade so be nice to the trees when your here.  Most camp sites have several spots for tents, and most have large paved parking pads for at least 2-3 good sized vehicles, several different types of sites from open sunny, to shady, some rocky, some in a meadow and some with tents spots down a hill.  You can hear the highway from the campground louder depending on what size you campng in but its not horrible, but the semis drag brakes can be loud if late at night.  They allow fires in fire pits currently when I visited.  I had to review because there was no good picture of the camp site layout I could find online except their hard to read size number map posted so I had to put a good map I found of the grounds, enjoy, camp, and have fun!! 4 stars cuz its far from lake, lots of sun, limited bathrooms and neighbors houses with lights on all night long.</review><pics>None< /pics>< resp>

<review>After my sister and I went to get a massage she really wanted to get something to eat. After looking on yelp she found SweetHoney Dessert. It's located in a small plaza with plenty of parking. Anyway walking in...the interior is super clean and modern. This place is a Hong Kong style dessert place with different types of Hong Kong desserts like sago and sticky rice.

I wasn't super particularly hungry but I found the coconut milk sago with palm something and ordered that. My sister then went to order the mango smoothie, coconut sago with a side of fresh cubed mango, and then some fried calamari rings.

Let me just say...the portions look a little small for the sago but they're filling. Do not worry! The mango smoothie is rich and super delicious. The calamari was a bit over cooked but this is a dessert place so my expectations weren't all that high.

The service was great and the server was super helpful with all our questions regarding the assortment of desserts. Also, if you check in on yelp you can get a discount off your entire order.

Side note my sister loved it so much she went back a couple days later with some other friends. I will probably go back if I'm in the area.</review>< pictures>

< review>
Saying you know everything about drums is a good thing, but be realistic. Guitar center does not hire experts, they hire kids that will work for minimum wage, and put up with us know it all musicians.
Are you going to work part time, for minimum wage, and smile when some kid comes in with his parents wanting a "piccolo china crash ride spash hat" or some other non-existant mumbo jumbo?
Will you keep smiling and figure out what the kid wants, or are you going to laugh at him, like you laugh at the kids in guitar center?
If they did hire you, and you go on a road tour, then what?
Guitar Center has different levels of shops. this is a little shop, then they have normal shops, and in some areas they have "pro-shops", where pros go in to talk to pro's and buy pro equipment. You will know it when you see it, due to the dozen latin percussion displays,the 3 DW kits on display, the rush 30th aniversary set on display, and the 48 piece gilbrater rack with 4 bass drums on a meter tall platform above it all.
Guitar Center is there to make money. If the stevenson ranch store is selling $100,000 a month in drums, expect guitar center to expand the drum area there.
Until then, be glad you have someplace close when you break your last set of drum sticks.< /review>

<user_name>Ami Jewell< /user_name><Time>1569535007226<//Time><Rating>5</Rating>< text>
This canyon is so beautiful and rich in history, and im happy to see that there's people breathing new life into the historical places that had been dormant for so long. Side note: I'm all for sharing the road, but if you're a bicyclist, please please please DON'T RIDE THE CANYON. Often the road is narrow, turns can be tight, corners blind. Big trucks come up and down this highway all day long, often crossing into the oncoming lane to make turns. If im coming around a corner and there's a truck in my lane coming at me and my choices are hit the truck, or hit you on your bike... I'm sorry buddy. We have a lot of great places to ride up here, beautiful valleys, epic mountain bike trails... the feather river canyon though, it's just not safe.<//text>

<review>They are more like 3.5 stars, but I feel generous. This analysis is before the strict instructions for lockdown.

I have always walked past this cafe, but until now, I have never managed to eat here. We came for an early brunch, and fortunately it's just not packed as usual yet. The outdoor seating is spacious and shady. We were sitting in a corner and the menu was conveniently taped to the table.

I got a smoked omelette of salmon and it was fine, but I should have demanded that the cream cheese be withheld. There's a really fluffy omelette.

Our waiter is very sweet, polite, and focused on protection. He asked us to ensure that when we order or when food is delivered to us, we wear our masks.

The restaurant is tiny and often has a wait on Friday mornings around 9am. Today we were lucky and were seated right away.
The eggs were nicely done (over hard as I requested). The bacon comes a little more cooked than I usually prefer but still tasty.

Overall I like this place and it's service.</review>

< Review>
You can smell the yummy goodness of what's in store for you long before you reach the door. Met a friend there for breakfast. We picked it based on Yelp reviews. In spite of the extensive, varied menu, I knew what I wanted as soon as I saw it: they had me at "goat cheese omelet". She ordered the smoked salmon omelette. Both were hearty proportions, and came with a choice of fruit or potatoes AND choice of toast or banana muffin. I think the highlight of the meal was the shredded- style hash browns. Total comfort food. Muffin was so-so... kind of dry and a little over baked, I thought.  I bake so I am really picky. My friend liked it, though. Place had a nice homey feel, and I was glad we were there early because it got busy later and there was a line to get in as we were leaving. They didn't pressure us to leave and we were able to sit and visit. On a nicer day, they have a nice outside area in front which is also good for people watching on the main California St. drag. Overall a great experience and I will definitely be back.<//Review>

Jill Chong< /name>
< Review>
Joanie's Cafe is such a nice place to have breakfast/brunch at! It has a homey vibe, seating indoors and out. The servers and staff were all very kind during my visit. It was a very comfortable environment.

I ordered the eggs benedict w/ smoked salmon, came with fresh fruit and my choice of hashbrown over fries. My boyfriend ordered the chorizo omelette with his choice of hashbrown and sourdough toast. I honestly loved my dish, the crunch and crispiness of the hashbrown the fresh fruit selection didn't go bad. And the main star of the dish, the smoked salmon benedict, had a very nice runny yolk and the sauce was light. I usually never had smoked salmon with my eggs benedict, so it was a nice change to my usual!

I'm never in the Palo Alto area, but if I'm back and want brunch then I'd definitely come back!< /Review>

I went to Joanie's early in the morning, so there was plenty of room, but the place filled up quickly. I ordered crepes and granola, but the portions are huge, so I left quite a bit on the plate. The granola was simply delicious. The crepes less so, but they were good. The coffee was also good.

<UserId.>110889359600338463075<//UserId.><user_name>Merry Yen<//user_name>< Time>
1352094110404</Time>
< Rating>
4<//Rating>
< Review>
We arrived at the peak of the brunch rush, and it was about a 30-40 minute wait to get a spot at the counter.  If you wanted a table then it may be a longer wait.
Service was courteous and efficient.  Decor is pleasant and bright.
The food was very very decent brunch food.  The omelet was well-cooked with lots of fresh ingredients; eggs and corned beef hash were both solid.  The Belgian waffle was a bit more chewy than my liking.  The hash browns were definitely the highlight - crispy on both sides, and well-seasoned.
We'd probably come back again, but next time we'll get here either earlier or later to avoid the brunch crunch.< /Review>

< text>
We went there for brunch, and all of the food we had was good to very good: Eggs Benedict, blueberry muffin, bacon, corned beef hash, and hashed browns. The exception were the scrambled eggs, which were dry and flavorless (maybe they use liquid eggs, yuck). The drinks were excellent. They served my wife's Americano as an espresso with pitchers of hot water and hot (!) cream so she could doctor it to her own satisfaction, something that we've never seen before and hope becomes a trend. They served my Mimosa with the remainder of a split of Blanc de Noir and a little pitcher of orange juice, so I was able to get something like three helpings out of it. And the service was excellent. Warning: portions are large. A very solid brunch option!</text>
